<a name="tr1929368"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000375">Robert Downey Jr.</a> kept food hidden all over the lab set and apparently nobody could find where it was, so they just let him continue doing it. In the movie, that's his actual food he's offering and when he was eating, it wasn't scripted. He was just hungry.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1696176">
<a name="tr1696176"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Reputedly a scene was filmed where during the final battle Captain America saves an old man trying to protect his grandchildren. He tells him to 'Get them to cover' but as he walks away the old man asks him "Cap, is that really you?'. He turns and, noting the man's World War II veteran lapel pin, trades salutes with him. As Captain America sprints away the children ask their grandfather 'Do you know him?' and he replies 'We ALL know him'.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1633649">
<a name="tr1633649"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


There were very few times that everyone was in town at once, but on one night when they were, <a href="/name/nm0262635">Chris Evans</a> sent them all a text message simply saying "Assemble" (the tagline to the movie), prompting a night out on the town. <a href="/name/nm0163988">Clark Gregg</a> has stated that this is his favorite text message that he has ever received.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1745383">
<a name="tr1745383"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Clint Barton (Hawkeye) is an ambidextrous archer (although <a href="/name/nm0719637">Jeremy Renner</a> is left handed). He is seen shooting right-handed in <a href="/title/tt0800369">Thor</a> (2011) and both left-handed and right-handed in this film.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1690665">
<a name="tr1690665"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


After Thor takes Loki off the Quinjet down on the mountain side, two large ravens fly by them as they are talking. In Norse mythology, their father, Odin, had two ravens, Huginn and Muninn, who would bring Odin information from Midgard (Earth).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1683757">
<a name="tr1683757"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000168">Samuel L. Jackson</a>'s role as Nick Fury in this film makes him the second actor (after <a href="/name/nm0413168">Hugh Jackman</a>, who has appeared in all the X-men movies) to play the same comic book superhero in five different movies.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1677267">
<a name="tr1677267"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


According to director <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a>, the original cut of the movie was over 3 hours long. About 30 minutes of the excised footage are included on the Blu-ray, most of which revolves around Steve Rogers (Captain America) struggling to adjust to the modern world. <a href="/name/nm0262635">Chris Evans</a> has since announced that these deleted scenes will be used for <a href="/title/tt1843866">The Return of the First Avenger</a> (2014).  </div>

<a name="tr1963606"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0262635">Chris Evans</a> was unsure about his character's line, "I understood that reference!" because he was worried that it would make audiences think that his character was unintelligent. However he was quickly comforted after he watched the movie with an audience and he saw that they found the line humorous as opposed to stupid.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1689204">
<a name="tr1689204"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The final end credit scene was added after <a href="/name/nm0000375">Robert Downey Jr.</a>. encouraged a scene rewrite: after Tony Stark falls back to Earth, he originally awakens and asks, "What's next?". Robert Downey Jr. thought the line could be more interesting, and the idea of going to a local shawarma restaurant was born. The scene was added one day after the global premiere. Since then, shawarma sales in Los Angeles, St. Louis, and Boston have reportedly skyrocketed.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1686627">
<a name="tr1686627"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000168">Samuel L. Jackson</a>'s Nick Fury is from the Ultimate Marvel Universe created in 2000 to re-imagine and update the Marvel heroes for the 21st century. Fury's likeness was actually based on Jackson, who gave Marvel permission to do so. Subsequently, based on that likeness and his star power, Jackson was cast as Fury for all Marvel superhero films owned by Marvel/Disney starting with <a href="/title/tt0371746">Iron Man</a> (2008).  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


The laboratory scene where Bruce Banner explains how he once attempted to commit suicide by shooting himself in the mouth is a direct reference to a deleted scene from <a href="/title/tt0800080">Der unglaubliche Hulk</a> (2008) where <a href="/name/nm0001570">Edward Norton</a>'s Bruce Banner tried to commit suicide in this manner out in the middle of Alaska's wilderness only to be stopped by his transformation into the Hulk.  </div>

The filmmakers secured the rights from Columbia Pictures to feature OsCorp Tower from <a href="/title/tt0948470">The Amazing Spider-Man</a> (2012) in New York. Unfortunately, by then digital rendering of the skyline was already complete and it could not appear.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1837559">
<a name="tr1837559"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


According to <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a>'s commentary, Bruce Banner's saying of Loki, "You can smell crazy on him", was a setup for when the Hulk faces off against Loki in Stark Tower. Originally, Loki was going to make multiple versions of himself and the only way the Hulk was going to discern where Loki was to smell them. Only the real Loki would have a scent.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1694466">
<a name="tr1694466"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0749263">Mark Ruffalo</a> claims to be the only actor to date (2012) to play both The Hulk and Bruce Banner in the same movie. Technically, both <a href="/name/nm0051509">Eric Bana</a> and <a href="/name/nm0001570">Edward Norton</a> have done motion capture work for their respective Hulks, but Ruffalo is the first actor to perform the Hulk live on set via performance capture.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1569203">
<a name="tr1569203"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


After Loki is brought on board the Helicarrier, Tony Stark can be seen wearing a <a href="/name/nm1277292">Black Sabbath</a> T-shirt. Black Sabbath is better known for their song "Iron Man." Although the song was not originally associated with the Marvel Comics character, it has since been referenced in the comics and the end of <a href="/title/tt0371746">Iron Man</a> (2008) when Tony quotes the lyric, "I am Iron Man."  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


When Natasha Romanoff and Bruce Banner are blasted to a lower deck of the Helicarrier, it triggers Banner's transformation into the Hulk. As he is transforming, he falls from a platform to the floor. On the floor is painted "WARNING CONTENTS UNDER PRESSURE" with small arrows, which happen to be pointing to Banner.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


Tony Stark/Iron Man casually refers to three of the other main characters - Loki, Thor and Hawkeye - as either movie characters or movie titles. He calls Loki <a href="/title/tt0184858">Wild Christmas</a> (2000), Thor <a href="/title/tt0102685">Gefährliche Brandung</a> (1991) and Hawkeye 'Legolas'.  </div>

The sound editor <a href="/name/nm0102110">Christopher Boyes</a> has stated that he went through a complicated process to craft the Hulk's voice. The final product "turned out to be [a combination of] <a href="/name/nm0749263">Mark Ruffalo</a>, some <a href="/name/nm0002073">Lou Ferrigno</a> and a little bit of me and two people from New Zealand."  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1868044">
<a name="tr1868044"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Originally <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a> had not intended the film to include supporting characters from the heroes' individual films, reasoning "You need to separate the characters from their support systems in order to create the isolation you need for a team." However, he eventually decided to cast <a href="/name/nm0001745">Stellan Skarsgård</a>, <a href="/name/nm0079273">Paul Bettany</a> and <a href="/name/nm0000569">Gwyneth Paltrow</a> (Paltrow was cast at <a href="/name/nm0000375">Robert Downey Jr.</a>'s insistence).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1519734">
<a name="tr1519734"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Director <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a> had earlier been considered to direct <a href="/title/tt0120903">X-Men</a> (2000) in the 1990s. A big fan of the X-Men, he even wrote a script, from which only two lines made it into the film. He wrote the story 'Gifted' for "Astonishing X-Men", which became the basis for <a href="/title/tt0376994">X-Men - Der letzte Widerstand</a> (2006).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1426826">
<a name="tr1426826"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0002073">Lou Ferrigno</a> contributed to the voice of the Hulk in this film. He has played the Hulk in almost every live-action version since 1978: he played the Hulk in <a href="/title/tt0077031">Der unglaubliche Hulk</a> (1978) and its subsequent three TV specials, and he voiced the Hulk in the big-screen <a href="/title/tt0800080">Der unglaubliche Hulk</a> (2008) in which he also played "security guard" - he also played a security guard in <a href="/title/tt0286716">Hulk</a> (2003). He also has voiced the Hulk in various animated productions.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1893095">
<a name="tr1893095"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Tony Stark tells Bruce Banner that he admires his work on anti-electron collisions. When electrons and anti-electrons (also known as positrons) collide, they annihilate each other and high-energy photons or gamma rays (the fictional means by which Bruce Banner became The Hulk) are produced in their place.  </div>

According to <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a>, the arrangement of the monitors on the helicarrier bridge were arranged to resemble the wings of the SHIELD logo. The eagle head can actually be seen at the foot of the conference round table at the end of the film when repairs are being made.  </div>

According to <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a>, the film is strongly influenced by the early 1960s Avengers comics, which he was a fan of while growing up: "In those comics these people shouldn't be in the same room let alone on the same team - and that is the definition of family."  </div>

<a href="/name/nm0000375">Robert Downey Jr.</a> initially pushed <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a> to make Tony Stark the lead: "I said, I need to be in the opening sequence, Tony needs to drive this thing. He was like, okay, let's try that. We tried it... and it didn't work, because this is a different sort of thing, everybody is just an arm of the octopus."  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1696585">
<a name="tr1696585"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The name "chitauri" originates from Zulu mythology and is used to describe a "serpent race from the sky". <a href="/name/nm2092839">Mark Millar</a>, the creator of "The Ultimates", took the name from the writings of <a href="/name/nm1079801">David Icke</a>, who argues that these "chitauri" are in fact aliens bent on dominating humanity.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr2156752">
<a name="tr2156752"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


This is the first film in the Marvel Cinematic Universe to debut the revised SHIELD logo. As compared to the more stylized eagle design on the logo (as seen in the opening scene at the dark energy research facility), the updated logo features a simplified eagle design (as seen on the flight deck and on the bridge of the helicarrier). This design will become the default SHIELD logo, as seen in Captain America: The Winter Soldier and Marvel's Agents of SHIELD.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1692471">
<a name="tr1692471"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Tony Stark's Acura roadster is neither the 2012 NSX Concept show car nor an actual prototype of the 2015 next-generation hybrid Acura NSX. It was custom designed specifically for the movie by Honda North America chief designer <a href="/name/nm5675609">Dave Marek</a>. The "donor car" was a 1991 NSX from Arizona with 252,000 miles on its odometer. The interior of the movie car is almost totally stock, and still has the original cassette tape player in the console.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr2047731">
<a name="tr2047731"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000375">Robert Downey Jr.</a> thought the scene when Iron Man regains consciousness could use a little snappier dialogue, so he requested that <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a> add some. One of the ones that made the cut (the Shawarma reference) is influenced by <a href="/name/nm0107183">Nicholas Brendon</a>'s (Xander from <a href="/title/tt0118276">Buffy - Im Bann der Dämonen</a> (1997)) interview. Nicholas mentions, 'Would anyone like to go get some Shawarma?'.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1633650">
<a name="tr1633650"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Tony Stark describes his group as "Earth's mightiest heroes, that kind of thing." This refers to the bold label that has appeared on "The Avengers" comic books since its 1963 publication. The phrase has also been used as the subtitle for <a href="/title/tt1626038">Die Avengers - Die mächtigsten Helden der Welt</a> (2010), the most recent animated series before the live-action Avengers film.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1685251">
<a name="tr1685251"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Thor spends most of this movie in his Asgardian armor but with bare arms, a nod to his early appearances in the comics. During his time on the Helicarrier, he is also seen without his cape, an allusion to his Ultimate Comics appearance.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1868042">
<a name="tr1868042"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Cinematographer <a href="/name/nm0568974">Seamus McGarvey</a> described the film's look as visceral and naturalistic: "We wanted this to feel immersive and did not want a comic-book look that might distance an audience. We moved the camera a lot on Steadicam, cranes and on dollies to create kinetic images; and we chose angles that were dramatic, like low angles, for heroic imagery."  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1578473">
<a name="tr1578473"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Since this film and <a href="/title/tt1300854">Iron Man 3</a> (2013) were originally part of a six-picture deal with Marvel and Paramount before the distribution rights were transferred to <a href="/name/nm0000370">Walt Disney</a> Pictures, it's the Paramount logo that appears in advertising and marketing as well as the beginning of this film. Although Paramount had no part in the production of "The Avengers", they still received a share of the box office grosses based on their original deal with Marvel. No reference to Disney is made until the very end of the closing credits, where it says "The Avengers" is "Distributed by Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures." The same is to be expected for "Iron Man 3".  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1570730">
<a name="tr1570730"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


This film holds an unusually high number of Academy Award nominees in the cast/crew for a comic book movie, or most movies for that matter: <a href="/name/nm0000375">Robert Downey Jr.</a>, <a href="/name/nm0000569">Gwyneth Paltrow</a>, <a href="/name/nm0000168">Samuel L. Jackson</a>, <a href="/name/nm0719637">Jeremy Renner</a>, <a href="/name/nm0749263">Mark Ruffalo</a>, director <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a>, and cinematographer <a href="/name/nm0568974">Seamus McGarvey</a>, possibly many others. This tops <a href="/title/tt0371746">Iron Man</a> (2008) and <a href="/title/tt1228705">Iron Man 2</a> (2010) which each had four acting nominees a piece. <a href="/title/tt1877832">X-Men: Zukunft ist Vergangenheit</a> (2014) broke the record with an impressive eight Oscar-nominated cast members.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


Loki is described as being a king in the world from which he came. Shortly after this when The Avengers ask for Loki's location in Germany, Loki is said to be at "22 Königstrasse", meaning 22 King Street.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


Several members of the cast participated in adaptations of comic book and/or graphic novel adaptations prior to the Marvel Cinematic Universe: <ul><li><a href="/name/nm0424060">Scarlett Johansson</a> has appeared in <a href="/title/tt0162346">Ghost World</a> (2001) and <a href="/title/tt0831887">The Spirit</a> (2008)</li><br/><br/><li><a href="/name/nm0262635">Chris Evans</a> appeared in <a href="/title/tt0120667">Fantastic Four</a> (2005), <a href="/title/tt0453556">Teenage Mutant Ninja Turtles</a> (2007), <a href="/title/tt0480255">The Losers</a> (2010) and <a href="/title/tt0446029">Scott Pilgrim gegen den Rest der Welt</a> (2010)</li><br/><br/><li><a href="/name/nm0000959">Powers Boothe</a> (who provides a cameo in the film) previously appeared in <a href="/title/tt0401792">Sin City</a> (2005)</li><br/><br/><li>and <a href="/name/nm0219206">Alexis Denisof</a> appeared in several DC productions beforehand.</li><br/><br/></ul> </div>

<div class="sodatext">


This is the third time <a href="/name/nm0424060">Scarlett Johansson</a> and <a href="/name/nm0262635">Chris Evans</a> have starred together in a film, both being in <a href="/title/tt0314498">Voll gepunktet</a> (2004) and <a href="/title/tt0489237">Nanny Diaries</a> (2007). This is also the second collaboration between <a href="/name/nm0000375">Robert Downey Jr.</a> and <a href="/name/nm0749263">Mark Ruffalo</a> since <a href="/title/tt0443706">Zodiac - Die Spur des Killers</a> (2007)  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1479550">
<a name="tr1479550"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0749263">Mark Ruffalo</a>'s performance of the Hulk is the first created by motion-capture. Previous live-action versions have had Bruce Banner and the Hulk be played by separate people (<a href="/name/nm0084642">Bill Bixby</a> and bodybuilder <a href="/name/nm0002073">Lou Ferrigno</a>), or were key-frame animated.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1479549">
<a name="tr1479549"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0749263">Mark Ruffalo</a> describes Bruce Banner as "a guy struggling with two sides of himself, the dark and the light; everything he does in his life is filtered through issues of control." He furthermore describes Banner's alter ego the Hulk as "a loose cannon - he's the teammate none of them are sure they want, it's like throwing a grenade into the middle of the group and hoping it turns out well!"  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1685250">
<a name="tr1685250"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The Chitauri appear in the first story arc of "The Ultimates," an alternate universe retelling of the origins of the Marvel superheroes. In the comics, their leader claims that they go by many names, including Skrulls. It was originally assumed that the reason for using The Chitauri instead of the Skrulls was that because Fox owns the rights to the Fantastic Four and their supporting characters however Marvel Studios' President of Production <a href="/name/nm0270559">Kevin Feige</a> stated in an interview that the film rights to the Skrulls are not owned by either Marvel Studios or Fox. The reason for them not being used was that <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a> did not want go the route of using shape-shifters in the first film.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1976134">
<a name="tr1976134"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Only the paint on Captain America's shield is scratched in the film. In the comics, his shield is made of an vibranium/iron alloy with a third mystery catalyst and can only be damaged by beings who possess nigh-ultimate power, such as Molecule Man, Rune King Thor, or Thanos w/ Infinity Gauntlet. The shield is otherwise impervious.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1868041">
<a name="tr1868041"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Cinematographer <a href="/name/nm0568974">Seamus McGarvey</a> shot the film in a 1.85:1 aspect ratio to cope with the varying heights: "We needed the height in the screen to be able to frame in all the characters like Hulk, Captain America and Black Widow, who is much smaller. We had to give them all precedence and width within the frame. Also, the final battle sequence was going to be this extravaganza in Manhattan, so the height and vertical scale of the buildings was going to be really important."  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1694757">
<a name="tr1694757"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The twelfth film to surpass the $1 billion mark worldwide, and the tenth to surpass the $400 million mark in the USA. It tied with <a href="/title/tt0499549">Avatar - Aufbruch nach Pandora</a> (2009) and <a href="/title/tt1201607">Harry Potter und die Heiligtümer des Todes - Teil 2</a> (2011) for surpassing the $1 billion mark worldwide in the fastest time (19 days) and set the record of surpassing the $400 million mark in the USA (14 days).  </div>

<a name="tr1689947"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


All the scenes filmed in Ohio were originally to be filmed in Michigan. Planned production was moved to Ohio when it was revealed that Michigan's film tax rebates were going to be revoked.  </div>

</div>
<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr2125071">
<a name="tr2125071"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The overall premise of the film is very similar to the pilot episode for the television cartoon "Justice League." (which is based on the DC comics counterpart) In both story lines, the team of super heroes bands together for the first time in the wake of a pending alien invasion.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1689862">
<a name="tr1689862"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The "wishbone" section of the helicarrier where Banner's lab is located is referred to in naval architecture as a "well deck"; it provides a sheltered docking area typically used for launching small boats or hover craft for carrying troops ashore.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr2304932">
<a name="tr2304932"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


According to the visual effects supervisor, director Joss Whedon disliked Iron Man's "tinkerbell pose" when flying. So he insisted that in this movie, the suit be equipped with a jet pack. This would allow his hands (guanlets) to be free, which, in turn offered those great "cowboy" poses, that were seen in the film  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1692438">
<a name="tr1692438"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The single-engine jet fighters are computer-rendered Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning IIs. F-35s appear briefly in several scenes, including a sequence of the airplane transitioning from forward flight to vectored-thrust hover mode to fire its 25mm cannon. The F-35 is still in development and will not even have basic combat capability until late 2015.  </div>

<a name="tr2309970"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Tony Stark (Robert Downey Jr)'s line "Do you guys want to get some shawarma?" is based on what Nicholas Brendon said after he auditioned for the role of Xander on Buffy the Vampire Slayer. According to Joss Whedon, Brendon said this line immediately after the audition and it won him the role.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1698521">
<a name="tr1698521"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Altough SHIELD possesses future technology such as the Helecarrier or the futuristic shuttles, some outdated aircraft can still be seen on the carrier. There is a huge number of Alpha-Jets, a German-French co-production that were put out of service by the German air forces in 1993. And we see some AV-8B Harrier II+, the night attack variant of the Sea Harrier, that is recognizable by its stretched nose and is still in service with the US Marine Corps. Finally there is the latest and most capable aircraft on board: the F-35 Lightning II that is about to be put in service by many air forces throughout the world.  </div>

<a id="cameo" name="cameo"></a>
<h4 class="li_group">Cameo </h4>
<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1686757">
<a name="tr1686757"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0498278">Stan Lee</a>: 

creator of such Marvel comics as the X-Men, Spider-Man, the Hulk, the Fantastic Four, Iron Man, Thor, and many others, is the old man being interviewed at the end of the New York battle montage who says: "Superheroes in New York? Give me a break!" and then returns to a game of chess with a fellow senior citizen. He also appeared in a deleted scene: after witnessing a waitress flirt with Steve Rogers, Lee's character says, "Ask for her number, you moron!"  </div>

<div class="list">
<a id="spoilers" name="spoilers"></a>
<h4 class="li_group">Spoilers </h4>
<div class="message_box small">
<div class="alert">
<p>The trivia items below may give away important plot points.</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1807932">
<a name="tr1807932"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


In the final end credit scene, Captain America is the only one not eating. That is because <a href="/name/nm0262635">Chris Evans</a> got a buzz cut and grew out his beard after The Avengers was done filming. He was called in later to do this extra scene and refused to shave off his beard due to having been filming <a href="/title/tt1706620">Snowpiercer</a> (2013) at the time, so they gave him the prosthetic jaw. He holds his hand over his face because the prosthetic made him look like he'd been attacked by a hive of angry bees. He also is unable to eat or talk with the prosthetic on. The wig he wears as Captain America is also quite clearly visible in certain shots of this scene.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr2124665">
<a name="tr2124665"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


It took Marvel three tries with the MPAA to grant the film a 'PG-13' instead of an 'R' rating because of Agent Coulson's death scene. Originally, Loki's staff was seen bursting through his chest; instead, a gruesome sound effect was added after Loki appears behind him, and then a quick-cut to Thor's reaction.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1728168">
<a name="tr1728168"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Besides the indication that "The Other" is talking to Thanos in the mid-credits scene (Thanos apparently being his master), there is another subtle nod to Thanos in Agent Coulson's remark to Loki that he lacks conviction and has an innate desire to lose - this, a subconscious desire to fail, is said (in the comics) to be Thanos' only weakness.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr2210547">
<a name="tr2210547"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


While Fury and the Avengers are arguing with each other on the Helicarrier, characters throw certain remarks that coincidentally foreshadow plot points in subsequent films: Steve asks Tony what he is without his armor, a topic deeply analyzed in <a href="/title/tt1300854">Iron Man 3</a> (2013); Fury aggressively chastised Thor about foreign species going to his planet to "blow stuff up", which comes into play in <a href="/title/tt1981115">Thor - The Dark Kingdom</a> (2013) with the invasion of Asgard by the Dark Elves. The most unassuming one (which is ironically translated into the biggest plot point in the whole cinematic universe) is when Bruce asks Natasha if Captain America is on threat watch, to which she replies "we all are". In <a href="/title/tt1843866">The Return of the First Avenger</a> (2014), Steve (and by extension, Natasha herself) becomes a fugitive of S.H.I.E.L.D. after the murder of Nick Fury. Natasha also mentions that S.H.I.E.L.D. monitors potential threats, which plays heavily into this film as well.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1695556">
<a name="tr1695556"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The character the minion is talking to in the credits is Thanos the Mad Titan, a major supervillain in the Marvel Universe. He is a cosmic mass murderer who is literally in love with the personification of Death, which is why he is smiling at the phrase, "To court death."  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1696427">
<a name="tr1696427"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a>: 
[Killing off a popular character] 
Agent Phil Coulson, a character who earned considerable popularity with fans through his appearance in almost all of the previous Marvel Studios films, is killed off in the middle of the film, giving the Avengers someone to avenge. On the commentary, Whedon says that it was not his decision to kill off Coulson in the film and that Marvel Studios' <a href="/name/nm0270559">Kevin Feige</a> made the call. Whedon would later bring Coulson back in the TV show <a href="/title/tt2364582">Marvel's Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D.</a> (2013).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1699663">
<a name="tr1699663"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Seconds before Hawkeye's attack on S.H.I.E.L.D's Helicarrier, Bruce Banner finds the Tesseract's location on the computer. This explains why later he arrives in New York during the invasion of the Chitauri after the Hulk (Banner transformed) fell to the ground from the helicarrier during Hawkeye's attack.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1868039">
<a name="tr1868039"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


According to <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a>, it was his decision to include Thanos in a post-credits scene: "He for me is THE most powerful and fascinating Marvel villain. He's the great-granddaddy of the badasses and he's in love with Death and I just think that's so cute. Somebody had to be in control and had to be behind Loki's work and I was like it's got to be Thanos."  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr2028199">
<a name="tr2028199"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


When Pepper and Tony are in their apartment going over digital plans to rebuild Stark tower, the quinjet isn't the only visible clue to an Avenger's headquarters. The logo of each Avenger in the film can be seen on the digital canvas and Captain America's shield is selected to reveal his quarters in the blueprint.  </div>

<a href="/name/nm1089991">Tom Hiddleston</a> describes Loki in this film as having evolved since <a href="/title/tt0800369">Thor</a> (2011): "How pleasant an experience is it to disappear into a wormhole that was created by some super-nuclear explosion of his own making? I think by the time Loki shows up he's seen a few things and has bigger things in mind than just his brother and Asgard...."  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1787024">
<a name="tr1787024"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Loki's staff which has a glowing blue gem in the spear head that allows him to control the minds of others. This is a possible reference to the Mind Gem, one of the six Infinity Gems used by Thanos the Mad Titan, shown in the post-credits scene.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1479553">
<a name="tr1479553"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Loki brings the Chitauri alien race to Earth to help him invade it. The Avengers are formed to prevent this from occurring. This is in keeping with the very first issue of their self-titled comic book series, in which Loki is responsible for manipulating a chain of disasters that bring the Avengers together in the first place.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1714097">
<a name="tr1714097"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


In the closing montage of the film, Pepper Potts shows Tony Stark a hologram of plans to rebuild the top of Stark Tower. In the hologram a Quinjet is clearly visible in the middle of the structure, one among several hints in the film to the possible use of Stark Tower as future Headquarters of the Avengers (as occurred in the comic series).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1692197">
<a name="tr1692197"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The decimation of Stark Tower during the final battle destroys the company logo, leaving only the illuminated "A" at the end of the film. This is a subtle nod (and potential sequel set-up) to the comics where the Avengers operate out of a giant building alternatively depicted as an "A" shaped building, or as a skyscraper with a giant "A" crowning the top.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1693273">
<a name="tr1693273"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


At the end of the film, when the news clip of the waitress appears on Nick Fury's computer screen it is listed as SHIELD File A113. "A113 is the room number of the animation classroom at CalArts. The A113 reference is a running gag in films made by Pixar Studios, starting with <a href="/title/tt0114709">Toy Story</a> (1995), a film partially written by <a href="/name/nm0923736">Joss Whedon</a> who wrote and directed <a href="/title/tt0848228">Marvel's The Avengers</a> (2012).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1690872">
<a name="tr1690872"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The Chitauri, the villainous alien race of this film, were the primary villains of the first volume of "The Ultimates", a comic book re-imagining of The Avengers. Subsequently Loki was one of the primary villains of the second volume of The Ultimates, though his appearance had nothing to do with the Chitauri.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr2344647">
<a name="tr2344647"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Lt. Colonel James Rhodes was considered to have a cameo in the after credit scene, where he is wearing his armor only to find out he came too late for the battle, and sits down with the Avengers; but the scene was thrown away to where they just show the Avengers eating. Rhodes will now have a key role conflict in Avengers: Age of Ultron(2015). His role will be very important in the film to where he could be one of the Avengers.  </div>
<div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a class="interesting-count-text" href="?item=tr2344647"> 11 of 12 found this interesting</a>
